# Investigation: Phantom In-Place Updates for Resources with Sensitive Attributes in Terraform

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/terraform--9658f9df (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/terraform--9658f9df (mirror of hashicorp/terraform)
**Task Type:** Deep Causal Chain (investigation only — no code fixes)

## Scenario

A Terraform user reports that `terraform plan` consistently shows resources "will be updated in-place" even though **no configuration changes** have been made. The phantom update appears for any resource that has provider-schema-defined sensitive attributes (e.g., `password`, `secret_key`).

The user is managing a VPN tunnel resource:

```hcl
resource "test_instance" "example" {
  ami      = "ami-12345"
  password = var.db_password  # provider schema marks 'password' as Sensitive: true
}
```

After a successful `terraform apply`, immediately running `terraform plan` shows:

```
  # test_instance.example will be updated in-place
  ~ resource "test_instance" "example" {
        id       = "i-abc123"
        # (1 unchanged attribute hidden)
    }

Plan: 0 to add, 1 to change, 0 to destroy.
```

There are **no actual attribute changes** — the before and after values are identical. The phantom diff occurs specifically for resources where the provider schema declares one or more attributes with `Sensitive: true`.

Additionally, `terraform show -json` on the state file shows that the `sensitive_values` section in the JSON output is **incomplete** — it lists sensitivity marks that came from variable references (e.g., `var.db_password` is a `sensitive` variable) but **omits** sensitivity marks from the provider schema itself (e.g., the `password` attribute is always sensitive regardless of how it's populated).

Running `terraform plan -refresh-only` also shows phantom changes, and `terraform import` followed by `terraform plan` shows even more phantom updates.

## Your Task

Investigate the root cause of why Terraform generates phantom in-place updates for resources with schema-sensitive attributes, and produce a report at `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

Your report MUST cover:

1. **How provider responses flow through the graph evaluator** — when `ReadResource` (refresh) or `PlanResourceChange` (plan) returns a value from the provider, how does `node_resource_abstract_instance.go` process that response? Specifically, examine `readResourceInstanceState()` (refresh path) and `plan()` (plan path) in `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`.

2. **The sensitivity mark gap** — the provider response comes back **without** any sensitivity marks (providers don't mark values; that's Terraform's responsibility). The code re-applies marks from the **prior state** (`priorPaths` from `AttrSensitivePaths`), but these only contain marks from sensitive variable references, NOT from the provider schema's `Sensitive: true` declarations.

3. **How state serialization records incomplete sensitivity** — when the instance object is written to state via `internal/states/instance_object.go`, `sensitive_attributes` in the state file only has paths from sensitive references, missing the schema-defined sensitive paths. Trace through how `AttrSensitivePaths` is populated and how `unmarkValueForStorage` extracts marks before state serialization.

4. **The evaluator's compensating workaround** — `internal/terraform/evaluate.go`'s `GetResource()` method was the ONLY place that applied schema marks (via `markProviderSensitiveAttributes()` or similar). This meant that when a value was read FROM state and decoded for expression evaluation, it would get schema marks added. But the value stored IN state never had those marks. This created an asymmetry.

5. **How the asymmetry produces phantom diffs** — the plan compares refreshed state (which has schema marks from the evaluator) against the planned state (which was built from provider response without schema marks). The mark difference causes the plan to detect a "change" even though the underlying values are identical. The diff is in the sensitivity metadata, not the attribute values themselves.

6. **The JSON output manifestation** — `internal/command/` layer functions that produce `terraform show -json` read `sensitive_attributes` from state, which is incomplete. This produces incorrect `sensitive_values` in JSON plan/state output, where schema-defined sensitive attributes are missing from the sensitivity map.

## Output Requirements

Write your investigation report to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with these sections:

```
# Investigation Report

## Summary
<1-2 sentence finding>

## Root Cause
<Specific file, function, and mechanism>

## Evidence
<Code references with file paths and line numbers>

<Ordered list: symptom → intermediate hops → root cause>

## Recommendation
<Fix strategy and diagnostic steps>
```

- Do NOT modify any source files
- Your job is investigation and analysis only
- The causal chain spans at least 4 packages: `internal/terraform/` (graph evaluation + marks), `internal/states/` (state serialization), `internal/command/` (JSON output), and the provider interaction boundary
- Focus on how `node_resource_abstract_instance.go` handles provider responses, how `marks.go` applies sensitivity, how `instance_object.go` serializes state, and how `evaluate.go` compensates

78-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive investigation of the phantom in-place update issue. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Investigation Complete

I've produced a detailed report at `/logs/agent/investigation.md` that covers:

### **Key Finding**
The phantom diffs occur because of **incomplete sensitivity mark persistence in state**. When resources are refreshed and stored:
- Only marks from sensitive variable references are saved
- Provider schema-defined sensitive attributes' marks are NOT saved
- Later, schema marks are applied dynamically at JSON output time
- This creates an apparent difference in sensitivity between before/after values

### **Root Cause Chain**
The issue spans across the entire sensitivity mark flow:

1. **Refresh Phase**: `node_resource_abstract_instance.go` (lines 620-722) extracts marks before sending to provider, but only saves variable marks back, not schema marks

2. **State Encoding**: `instance_object.go` (line 98) encodes only the marks present in the value, which are incomplete

3. **State Decoding**: `instance_object_src.go` (lines 89-90) restores only the incomplete marks

4. **Compensating Layer**: `evaluate.go`'s `GetResource()` (lines 714-723) applies schema marks when reading for expression evaluation, but these aren't captured in the plan

5. **JSON Output**: `jsonplan/plan.go` (lines 418-420, 446-449) applies schema marks on-the-fly for display, creating asymmetry

### **Affected Components**
- `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go` - Refresh & plan paths
- `internal/states/instance_object.go` - State serialization  
- `internal/states/instance_object_src.go` - State deserialization
- `internal/terraform/evaluate.go` - Expression evaluation (compensating)
- `internal/command/jsonplan/plan.go` - JSON output
... (truncated)

for %q during refresh\\n\", n.ResolvedProvider.Provider, n.Addr)\n690: \t}\n691: \n692: \tret := state.DeepCopy()\n693: \tret.Value = newState\n694: \tret.Private = resp.Private\n695: \n696: \t// We and represent \"drift\" from\n699: \t// external changes which will be handled by the subsequent plan.\n700: \tif errs := objchange.AssertObjectCompatible(schema, priorVal, ret.Value); len(errs) > 0 \t\tfor _, err := range errs {\n704: \t\t\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"\\n      - %s\", tfdiags.FormatError(err))\n705: \t\t}\n706: \t\tlog.Print(buf.String())\n707: \t}\n708: \n709: \t// Call post-refresh hook\n710: \tdiags = diags.Append(ctx.Hook(func(h Hook) (HookAction, error) {\n711: \t\treturn h.PostRefresh(absAddr, deposedKey, priorVal, ret.Value)\n712: \t}))\n713: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n714: \t\treturn ret, diags\n715: \t}\n716: \n717: \t// Mark the value if necessary\n718: \tif len(priorPaths) > 0 {\n719: \t\tret.Value = ret.Value.MarkWithPaths(priorPaths)\n720: \t}\n721: \n722: \treturn ret, diags\n723: }\n724: \n725: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) plan(\n726: \tctx EvalContext,\n727: \tplannedChange *plans.ResourceInstanceChange,\n728: \tcurrentState *states.ResourceInstanceObject,\n729: \tcreateBeforeDestroy bool,\n730: \tforceReplace []addrs.AbsResourceInstance,\n731: ) (*plans.ResourceInstanceChange, *states.ResourceInstanceObject, instances.RepetitionData, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n732: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n733: \tvar keyData instances.RepetitionData\n734: \n735: \tresource := n.Addr.Resource.Resource\n736: \tprovider, providerSchema, err := getProvider(ctx, n.ResolvedProvider)\n737: \tif err != nil {\n738: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags.Append(err)\n739: \t}\n740: \n741: \tschema, _ := generate it now.\n749: \tif n.Config == nil {\n750: \t\t// This shouldn't happen. A node that isn't generating config should\n751: \t\t// have embedded config, and the rest of Terraform should enforce this.\n752: \t\t// If, however, we didn't do things correctly the next line will panic,\n753: \t\t// so let's not do that and return an error message with more context.\n754: \n755: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n756: \t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n757: \t\t\t\"Resource has no configuration\",\n758: \t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\"Terraform attempted to process a resource at %s that has no configuration. This is a bug in Terraform; please report it!\", n.Addr.String())))\n759: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n760: \t}\n761: \n762: \tconfig := *n.Config\n763: \n764: \tcheckRuleSeverity := tfdiags.Error\n765: \tif n.preDestroyRefresh {\n766: \t\tcheckRuleSeverity = tfdiags.Warning\n767: \t}\n768: \n769: \tif plannedChange != nil {\n770: \t\t// If we already planned the action, we stick to that plan\n771: \t\tcreateBeforeDestroy = plannedChange.Action == plans.CreateThenDelete\n772: \t}\n773: \n774: \t// Evaluate the configuration\n775: \tforEach, _ := evaluateForEachExpression(n.Config.ForEach, ctx)\n776: \n777: \tkeyData = EvalDataForInstanceKey(n.ResourceInstanceAddr().Resource.Key, forEach)\n778: \n779: \tcheckDiags := evalCheckRules(\n780: \t\taddrs.ResourcePrecondition,\n781: \t\tn.Config.Preconditions,\n782: \t\tctx, n.Addr, keyData,\n783: \t\tcheckRuleSeverity,\n784: \t)\n785: \tdiags = diags.Append(checkDiags)\n786: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n787: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags // failed preconditions prevent further evaluation\n788: \t}\n789: \n790: \t// If we have a previous plan and the action was a noop, then the only\n791: \t// reason we're in this method was to evaluate the preconditions. The config was\n831: \t// statically validated early on, but there may have been unknown values\n832: \t// which the provider could not validate at the time.\n833: \t//\n834: \t// TODO: It would be more correct to validate the config after\n835: \t// ignore_changes has been applied, but the current implementation cannot\n836: \t// exclude computed-only attributes when given the `all` option.\n837: \n838: \t// we must unmark and use the original config, since the ignore_changes\n839: \t// handling below needs access to the marks.\n840: \tunmarkedConfigVal, _ := origConfigVal.UnmarkDeep()\n841: \tvalidateResp := provider.ValidateResourceConfig(\n842: \t\tproviders.ValidateResourceConfigRequest{\n843: \t\t\tTypeName: n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type,\n844: \t\t\tConfig:   unmarkedConfigVal,\n845: \t\t},\n846: \t)\n847: \tdiags = diags.Append(validateResp.Diagnostics.InConfigBody(config.Config, n.Addr.String()))\n848: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n849: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n850: \t}\n851: \n852: \t// ignore_changes is meant to only apply to the configuration, so it must\n853: \t// be applied before we generate a plan. of this is where providers attempt to obfuscate\n980: \t\t// config data by turning the config value into a hash and storing the\n981: \t\t// hash value in the state. the\n984: \t\t// ignored values once more.\n985: \t\t// A nil schema is passed to processIgnoreChanges to indicate that we\n986: \t\t// don't want to fixup a config value according to the schema because this is a Create action.\n1014: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n1015: \t\t\t}\n1016: \n1017: \t\t\tpriorChangedVal, priorPathDiags := hcl.ApplyPath(unmarkedPriorVal, path, nil)\n1018: \t\t\tplannedChangedVal, plannedPathDiags := hcl.ApplyPath(plannedNewVal, path, nil)\n1019: \t\t\tif plannedPathDiags.HasErrors() && priorPathDiags.HasErrors() {\n1020: \t\t\t\t// This means the path was invalid in both the prior and new\n1021: \t\t\t\t// values, which is an error with the provider itself.\n1022: \t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n1023: path,\n1028: \t\t\t\t\t),\n1029: \t\t\t\t))\n1030: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n1031: \t\t\t}\n1032: \n1033: \t\t\t// Make sure we have valid Values for both values.\n1034: \t\t\t// Note: if the opposing value was of the type\n1035: \t\t\t// cty.DynamicPseudoType, the type assigned here may not exactly\n1036: \t\t\t// match the schema. This is fine here, since we're only going to\n1037: \t\t\t// check for equality, but if the NullVal is to be used, we need to\n1038: \t\t\t// check the schema for th true type.\n1039: \t\t\tswitch {\n1040: \t\t\tcase priorChangedVal == cty.NilVal && plannedChangedVal == cty.NilVal:\n1041: \t\t\t\t// this should never happen without ApplyPath errors above\n1042: \t\t\t\tpanic(\"requires replace path returned 2 nil values\")\n1043: \t\t\tcase priorChangedVal == cty.NilVal:\n1044: \t\t\t\tpriorChangedVal = cty.NullVal(plannedChangedVal.Type())\n1045: \t\t\tcase plannedChangedVal == cty.NilVal:\n1046: \t\t\t\tplannedChangedVal = cty.NullVal(priorChangedVal.Type())\n1047: \t\t\t}\n1048: \n1049: \t\t\t// Unmark for this value for the equality test. should\n1078: \t\t// prevent us from getting here in that case.\n1079: \t}\n1080: \n1081: \t// Unmark for this test for value equality.\n1082: \teqV := plans.ResourceInstanceChangeActionReason\n1087: \tswitch {\n1088: \tcase priorVal.IsNull():\n1089: \t\taction = plans.Create\n1090: \tcase eq && !matchedForceReplace:\n1091: \t\taction = \t\t\tactionReason = plans.ResourceInstanceReplaceBecauseCannotUpdate\n1106: \t\t}\n1107: \tdefault:\n1108: \t\taction = plans.Update\n1109: \t\t// \"Delete\" is never chosen here, because deletion plans are always\n1110: \t\t// created more directly elsewhere, such as in \"orphan\" handling.\n1111: \t}\n1112: \n1113: \tif action.IsReplace() {\n1114: \t\t// In this strange situation we want to that has all the computed values on it.\n1118: \t\t//\n1119: \t\t// Therefore we'll ask the provider to plan again here, giving it\n1120: \t\t// a null object for the prior, and then we'll meld that with the\n1121: \t\t// _actual_ prior state to produce a correctly-shaped replace change.\n1122: \t\t// The resulting change should show any computed attributes changing\n1123: \t\t// from known prior values to unknown values, unless the provider is\n1124: \t\t// able to predict new values for any of these computed attributes.\n1125: \t\tnullPriorVal := cty.NullVal(schema.ImpliedType())\n1126: \n1127: \t\t// Since there is no prior state to compare after replacement, we need\n1128: \t\t// a new unmarked config from our original with no ignored values.\n1129: \t\tunmarkedConfigVal := origConfigVal\n1130: \t\tif origConfigVal.ContainsMarked() {\n1131: \t\t\tunmarkedConfigVal, _ = origConfigVal.UnmarkDeep()\n1132: \t\t}\n1133: \n1134: \t\t// create a new proposed value from the null state and the config\n1135: \t\tproposedNewVal = objchange.ProposedNew(schema, nullPriorVal, unmarkedConfigVal)\n1136: \n1137: \t\tif n.override != nil {\n1138: \t\t\t// In this case, we are always creating the resource so we don't\n1139: \t\t\t// do any validation, and just call out to the mocking library.\n1140: \t\t\toverride, overrideDiags := mocking.PlanComputedValuesForResource(proposedNewVal, schema)\n1141: \t\t\tresp = providers.PlanResourceChangeResponse{\n1142: \t\t\t\tPlannedState: override,\n1143: \t\t\t\tDiagnostics: \t\t\t\tPriorPrivate:     plannedPrivate,\n1152: \t\t\t\tProviderMeta:     metaConfigVal,\n1153: \t\t\t})\n1154: \t\t}\n1155: \t\t// We need to tread carefully here, since if there are any nil, keyData, diags\n1183: \t\t}\n1184: \t}\n1185: \n1186: \t// If our prior value was tainted then we actually want this to appear\n1187: \t// as a replace change, even though so far we've been treating it as a\n1188: \t// create.\n1189: \tif action == plans.Create && !priorValTainted.IsNull() {\n1190: \t\tif createBeforeDestroy {\n1191: \t\t\taction = plans.CreateThenDelete\n1192: \t\t} planned\n1203: \t// value before comparison. The one case where a provider is allowed to\n1204: \t// return a different value from the configuration is when a config change\n1205: \t// is not functionally significant and the prior state can be returned. plan\n1213: \t// phases, whereas we're now in the apply phase) and it was for a replace,\n1214: \t// we've already deleted the original object from state by the time we\n1215: \t// get here and so we would've ended up with a _create_ action this time,\n1216: \t// which we now need to paper over to get a result consistent with what\n1217: \t// we originally intended.\n1218: \tif plannedChange != nil {\n1219: \t\tprevChange := *plannedChange\n1220: \t\tif prevChange.Action.IsReplace() && action == plans.Create {\n1221: \t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] plan: %s treating Create change as %s change to match with earlier plan\", n.Addr, prevChange.Action)\n1222: \t\t\taction = prevChange.Action\n1223: \t\t\tpriorVal = prevChange.Before\n1224: \t\t}\n1225: \t}\n1226: \n1227: \t// Call post-refresh hook\n1228: \tdiags = diags.Append(ctx.Hook(func(h Hook) (HookAction, error) {\n1229: \t\treturn h.PostDiff(n.Addr, addrs.NotDeposed, action, priorVal, plannedNewVal)\n1230: \t}))\n1231: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n1232: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n1233: \t}\n1234: \n1235: \t// Update our return plan\n1236: \tplan := &plans.ResourceInstanceChange{\n1237: \t\tAddr: \t\t// object's value is not yet complete. attr.Computed && !attr.Optional {\n1299: \t\t\t\treturn cty.NullVal(v.Type()), nil\n1300: \t\t\t}\n1301: \n1302: \t\t\treturn v, nil\n1303: \t\t})\n1304: \n1305: \t\treturn ret, nil\n1306: \t}\n1307: \n1308: \tif prior.IsNull() || config.IsNull() {\n1309: \t\t// Ignore changes doesn't apply when we're creating for the first time.\n1310: \t\t// Proposed should never be null here, but if it is then }\n1318: \n1319: // Convert the hcl.Traversal values we get form the configuration to the\n1320: // cty.Path values we need to operate on the cty.Values\n1321: func traversalsToPaths(traversals []hcl.Traversal) []cty.Path {\n1322: \tpaths := make([]cty.Path, len(traversals))\n1323: \tfor i, traversal := range traversals {\n1324: \t\tpath := traversalToPath(traversal)\n1325: \t\tpaths[i] = path\n1326: \t}\n1327: \treturn paths\n1328: }\n1329: \n1330: func traversalToPath(traversal hcl.Traversal) cty.Path {\n1331: \tpath := make(cty.Path, len(traversal))\n1332: \tfor si, step := range traversal {\n1333: \t\tswitch ts := step.(type) {\n1334: \t\tcase hcl.TraverseRoot:\n1335: \t\t\tpath[si] = cty.GetAttrStep{\n1336: \t\t\t\tName: ts.Name,\n1337: \t\t\t}\n1338: \t\tcase hcl.TraverseAttr:\n1339: \t\t\tpath[si] = cty.GetAttrStep{\n1340: \t\t\t\tName: ts.Name,\n1341: \t\t\t}\n1342: \t\tcase hcl.TraverseIndex:\n1343: \t\t\tpath[si] = cty.IndexStep{\n1344: \t\t\t\tKey: ts.Key,\n1345: \t\t\t}\n1346: \t\tdefault:\n1347: \t\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"unsupported traversal step %#v\", step))\n1348: \t\t}\n1349: \t}\n1350: \treturn path\n1351: }\n1352: \n1353: func processIgnoreChangesIndividual(prior, config cty.Value, ignoreChangesPath []cty.Path) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n1354: \ttype ignoreChange struct {\n1355: \t\t// Path is the full path, minus any trailing map index\n1356: \t\tpath cty.Path\n1357: \t\t// Value is the value we are to retain at the above path. If there is a\n1358: \t\t// key value, this must be a map and the desired value will be at the\n1359: \t\t// key index.\n1360: \t\tvalue cty.Value\n1361: \t\t// Key is the index key if the ignored path ends in a map index.\n1362: \t\tkey cty.Value\n1363: \t}\n1364: \tvar ignoredValues []ignoreChange\n1365: \n1366: \t// Find the actual changes first and store them in the ignoreChange struct.\n1367: \t// If the change was to a map value, and the key doesn't exist in the\n1368: \t// config, it would never be visited in the transform walk.\n1369: \tfor _, icPath := range ignoreChangesPath {\n1370: \t\tkey := cty.NullVal(cty.String)\n1371: \t\t// check for a map index, since maps are the only structure where we\n1372: \t\t// could have invalid path steps.\n1373: \t\tlast, ok := icPath[len(icPath)-1].(cty.IndexStep)\n1374: \t\tif ok {\n1375: \t\t\tif last.Key.Type() == cty.String {\n1376: \t\t\t\ticPath = icPath[:len(icPath)-1]\n1377: \t\t\t\tkey = last.Key\n1378: \t\t\t}\n1379: \t\t}\n1380: \n1381: \t\t// The structure should have been validated already, and we already\n1382: \t\t// trimmed the trailing map index. This means that the change is stored\n1396: \t\t// here even if our ignored key doesn't change. That is OK since it\n1397: \t\t// won't cause any changes in the transformation, but allows us to skip\n1398: \t\t// breaking up the maps and checking for key existence here too.\n1399: \t\tif !p.RawEquals(c) {\n1400: \t\t\t// there a change to ignore at this path, store the prior value\n1401: \t\t\tignoredValues = append(ignoredValues, ignoreChange{icPath, p, key})\n1402: \t\t}\n1403: \t}\n1404: \n1405: \tif len(ignoredValues) == 0 {\n1406: \t\treturn config, nil\n1407: \t}\n1408: \n1409: \tret, _ := cty.Transform(config, func(path cty.Path, v cty.Value) (cty.Value, error) {\n1410: \t\t// Easy path for when we are only matching the entire value. The only\n1411: \t\t// values we break up for inspection are maps.\n1412: \t\tif !v.Type().IsMapType() {\n1413: \t\t\tfor _, ignored := range ignoredValues {\n1414: \t\t\t\tif to accumulate the values\n1421: \t\t// key-by-key.\n1422: \n1423: \t\tif !v.IsNull() && !v.IsKnown() {\n1424: \t\t\t// since v is not known, we cannot ignore individual keys\n1425: \t\t\treturn v, \n1432: \t\t// The configMap is the current configuration value, which we will\n1433: \t\t// mutate based on the ignored paths and the prior map value.\n1434: \t\tvar configMap accumulating values.\n1451: \t\t\t\treturn ignored.value, nil\n1452: \t\t\t}\n1453: \t\t\t// Now we know we are ignoring a specific index of this map, so get\n1454: \t\t\t// the config map and modify, add, or remove the desired key.\n1455: \n1456: \t\t\t// We also need to create a prior map, so we can check for\n1457: \t\t\t// existence while getting the value, because Value.Index will\n1458: \t\t\t// return null for a key with a null value and for a non-existent\n1459: \t\t\t// key.\n1460: \t\t\tvar priorMap map[string]cty.Value\n1461: \n1462: \t\t\t// We need to drop the marks from the \t\t\tdefault:\n1483: \t\t\t\tconfigMap[key] = priorElem\n1484: \t\t\t}\n1485: \t\t}\n1486: \n1487: \t\tvar newVal cty.Value\n1488: \t\tswitch {\n1489: \t\tcase len(configMap) > 0:\n1490: \t\t\tnewVal \t\t}\n1502: \n1503: \t\treturn newVal, nil\n1504: \t})\n1505: \treturn ret, nil\n1506: }\n1507: \n1508: // readDataSource handles everything needed to call ReadDataSource on the provider.\n1509: // A not wholly known.\\n\\nThis is a bug in the provider, which should be reported in the provider's own issue tracker.\",\n1621: \t\t\t\tn.ResolvedProvider, n.Addr,\n1622: \t\t\t),\n1623: \t\t))\n1624: \n1625: \t\t// We'll still save the object, but we need to eliminate any unknown\n1626: \t\t// values first because we can't serialize them in the state file.\n1627: \t\t// Note that this may cause diags.Err())\n1640: \t}))\n1641: \n1642: \treturn newVal, diags\n1643: }\n1644: \n1645: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) providerMetas(ctx EvalContext) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n1646: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n1647: \tmetaConfigVal := cty.NullVal(cty.DynamicPseudoType)\n1648: \n1649: \t_, providerSchema, err := getProvider(ctx, n.ResolvedProvider)\n1650: \tif err != nil resource lifecycle:\n1674: // either actually reading from the data source or generating a plan to do so.\n1675: //\n1676: // currentState is the current state for the data source, and the new state is\n1677: // returned. If we needed to read a new\n1679: // value, but it still matches the previous state, then we can record a NoNop\n1680: // change. tfdiags.Diagnostics\n1684: \tvar keyData instances.RepetitionData\n1685: \tvar configVal cty.Value\n1686: \n1687: \t_, providerSchema, err := getProvider(ctx, n.ResolvedProvider)\n1688: \tif err != Normally, this would\n1728: \t\t// cancel the entire plan and this error message would bubble its way\n1729: \t\t// back up to the user.\n1730: \t\t//\n1731: \t\t// But, if we are in a check block then we don't want this data block to\n1732: \t\t// cause the plan to fail. \t\t\t\tctx.Checks().ReportCheckResult(check.Addr().Absolute(n.Addr.Module), addrs.CheckDataResource, 0, checks.StatusPass)\n1746: \t\t\t}\n1747: \t\t}()\n1748: \t}\n1749: \n1750: \tconfigKnown := main part of the data resource lifecycle: either\n1956: // actually reading from the data source or generating a plan to do so.\n1957: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) applyDataSource(ctx (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) evalApplyProvisioners(ctx EvalContext, state *states.ResourceInstanceObject, createNew bool, when configs.ProvisionerWhen) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n2059: \tvar diags hook\n2100: \treturn diags.Append(ctx.Hook(func(h Hook) (HookAction, error) {\n2101: \t\treturn h.PostProvisionInstance(n.Addr, state.Value)\n2102: \t}))\n2103: }\n2104: \n2105: // filterProvisioners tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n2129: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n2130: \n2131: \t// this self is only used for destroy provisioner evaluation, and must\n2132: \t// refer to the last known value of the attr.Computed && !attr.Optional {\n1299: \t\t\t\treturn cty.NullVal(v.Type()), nil\n1300: \t\t\t}\n1301: \n1302: \t\t\treturn v, nil\n1303: \t\t})\n1304: \n1305: \t\treturn ret, nil\n1306: \t}\n1307: }\n1318: \n1319: // Convert the hcl.Traversal values we get form the configuration to the\n1320: // cty.Path values we need to operate on the cty.Values\n1321: func traversalsToPaths(traversals []hcl.Traversal) []cty.Path {\n1322: \tpaths := make([]cty.Path, len(traversals))\n1323: \tfor i, traversal := range traversals {\n1324: \t\tpath := traversalToPath(traversal)\n1325: \t\tpaths[i] = ts.Key,\n1345: \t\t\t}\n1346: \t\tdefault:\n1347: \t\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"unsupported traversal step %#v\", step))\n1348: \t\t}\n1349: \t}\n1350: \treturn path\n1351: ",

  "content": "# Investigation Report: Phantom In-Place Updates for Resources with Sensitive Attributes\n\n## Summary\n\nTerraform generates phantom in-place update diffs for resources with provider-schema-defined sensitive attributes because of an asymmetry in how sensitivity marks flow through the system. The issue stems from **incomplete sensitivity mark persistence in state**: when resource values are refreshed and stored, only marks from sensitive variable references are saved, not marks from the provider schema itself. During plan generation, schema marks are applied dynamically to the JSON output for display purposes, creating an apparent difference in sensitivity between before and after values even though the underlying attribute values are identical.\n\n---\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**Incomplete sensitivity mark storage at state serialization boundary.**\n\nThe root cause is located in the **state refresh-to-storage pipeline**, specifically:\n\n1. **`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`, `refresh()` method (lines 620-722)**: When a resource is refreshed from the provider, marks extracted before sending to the provider (`priorPaths` at line 625) only contain marks from sensitive variables (e.g., `var.db_password` marked as sensitive). These are **not** the provider schema's declared sensitive attributes.\n\n2. **`internal/states/instance_object.go`, `Encode()` method (line 98)**: When encoding the refreshed value for storage, `UnmarkDeepWithPaths()` extracts **only the marks currently on the value**. Since schema-defined sensitive marks were never added to the refreshed value (the provider returns unmarked values and only variable marks are reapplied), the schema marks are **not** present in the encoded state.\n\n3. **`internal/states/instance_object_src.go`, `Decode()` method (lines 89-90)**: When decoding from state, only the marks that were stored (`AttrSensitivePaths`) are reapplied. These lack schema-defined marks.\n\n4. **`internal/terraform/evaluate.go`, `GetResource()` method (lines 714-723)**: This is the **compensating workaround** that masks the underlying issue. When reading resource values for expression evaluation during planning, the code explicitly applies schema marks if the schema contains sensitive attributes. This creates the asymmetry: values read **via GetResource** have schema marks added, but values read **directly from state** in the plan path do not.\n\n5. **`internal/command/jsonplan/plan.go`, `MarshalResourceChange()` method (lines 417-420, 446-449)**: When generating JSON output for display, schema marks are applied on-the-fly to both before and after values. This compounds the issue: the before value appears to have sensitivity marks that were never stored in the plan itself.\n\n---\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Code References\n\n**1. Refresh Path \u2013 Incomplete Mark Extraction (node_resource_abstract_instance.go:620-722)**\n\n```go\n// Line 623-626: Extract marks BEFORE sending to provider\nvar priorPaths []cty.PathValueMarks\nif priorVal.ContainsMarked() {\n    priorVal, priorPaths = priorVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n}\n// priorPaths only contains marks from sensitive variables, NOT schema\n\n// Line 717-720: Reapply marks AFTER provider returns\nif len(priorPaths) > 0 {\n    ret.Value = ret.Value.MarkWithPaths(priorPaths)\n}\n// Schema marks are NOT reapplied here\n```\n\n**Issue**: `priorPaths` only has marks from sensitive variable references. Provider schema declares sensitive attributes are never added at this point.\n\n---\n\n**2. State Encoding \u2013 Missing Schema Marks (instance_object.go:94-137)**\n\n```go\nfunc (o *ResourceInstanceObject) Encode(ty cty.Type, schemaVersion uint64) (*ResourceInstanceObjectSrc, error) {\n    // Line 98: Extract existing marks\n    val, pvm := o.Value.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n\n    // ... process value ...\n\n    // Line 131: Save only the marks that are on the value\n    AttrSensitivePaths:  pvm,  // Missing schema marks!\n}\n```\n\n**Issue**: Only marks present in the value are persisted. Schema-defined sensitive marks are never in the value because the refresh path never adds them.\n\n---\n\n**3. State Decoding \u2013 Restore Incomplete Marks (instance_object_src.go:77-104)**\n\n```go\nfunc (os *ResourceInstanceObjectSrc) Decode(ty cty.Type) (*ResourceInstanceObject, error) {\n    val, err := ctyjson.Unmarshal(os.AttrsJSON, ty)\n    if os.AttrSensitivePaths != nil {\n        val = val.MarkWithPaths(os.AttrSensitivePaths)  // Only has variable marks\n    }\n    return &ResourceInstanceObject{Value: val, ...}, nil\n}\n```\n\n**Issue**: Reapplies only the incomplete marks that were stored.\n\n---\n\n**4. Evaluator Compensation \u2013 Schema Marks Applied at Expression Evaluation Time (evaluate.go:714-723)**\n\n```go\n// When reading from state for planned resources (lines 714-723)\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    var marks []cty.PathValueMarks\n    val, marks = val.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n    marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(val, nil)...)  // ADD schema marks here\n    val = val.MarkWithPaths(marks)\n}\ninstances[key] = val\n```\n\n**Issue**: This is a compensating mechanism that adds schema marks during **evaluation** (when reading from state for expression purposes), but these marks are **not** part of the planned change or state storage. This is the ONLY place schema marks are applied in the normal flow.\n\n---\n\n**5. JSON Output Generation \u2013 Dynamic Schema Mark Addition (jsonplan/plan.go:417-420, 446-449)**\n\n```go\n// For Before value (line 417-425):\nmarks := rc.BeforeValMarks  // Only has variable marks from the plan\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(changeV.Before, nil)...)  // Add schema marks here\n}\nbs := jsonstate.SensitiveAsBool(changeV.Before.MarkWithPaths(marks))\nbeforeSensitive, err := ctyjson.Marshal(bs, bs.Type())\n\n// For After value (line 446-449):\nmarks := rc.AfterValMarks  // Only has variable marks from the plan\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(changeV.After, nil)...)  // Add schema marks here\n}\nas := jsonstate.SensitiveAsBool(changeV.After.MarkWithPaths(marks))\nafterSensitive, err := ctyjson.Marshal(as, as.Type())\n```\n\n**Issue**: Schema marks are applied at JSON output time, making the before value appear to have sensitivity information that was never persisted in the plan. The difference in before vs. after sensitivity (in marks only, not in values) appears as a change to the user.\n\n---\n\n**6. Plan Phase \u2013 Incomplete Mark Comparison (node_resource_abstract_instance.go:1208-1210)**\n\n```go\n// Check if marks differ even though values are equal\nif action == plans.NoOp && !marksEqual(filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths), priorPaths) {\n    action = plans.Update\n}\n```\n\n**Issue**: This compares `unmarkedPaths` (marks from config) against `priorPaths` (marks from state, missing schema marks). Neither has schema marks, so for schema-sensitive attributes with no variable marks, they appear equal when they shouldn't.\n\n---\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`** \u2013 Refresh path, plan path:\n   - `refresh()` method: Extracts and reapplies incomplete marks\n   - `plan()` method: Uses incomplete marks for comparison\n   - Does not apply schema marks to prior values\n\n2. **`internal/states/instance_object.go`** \u2013 State serialization:\n   - `Encode()` method: Serializes incomplete marks to state file\n\n3. **`internal/states/instance_object_src.go`** \u2013 State deserialization:\n   - `Decode()` method: Restores incomplete marks from state\n\n4. **`internal/terraform/evaluate.go`** \u2013 Expression evaluation:\n   - `GetResource()` method: Applies schema marks when reading state for evaluation (compensating mechanism)\n\n5. **`internal/command/jsonplan/plan.go`** \u2013 JSON plan output:\n   - `MarshalResourceChange()` method: Dynamically applies schema marks at output time\n\n6. **`internal/terraform/marks.go`** \u2013 Utility functions:\n   - `marksEqual()`: Used for comparing incomplete mark sets\n   - `filterMarks()`: Filters inapplicable marks\n\n---\n\n## Causal Chain\n\n```\n1. SYMPTOM: terraform plan shows phantom in-place update even with no config changes\n   \u2193\n2. User sees \"will be updated in-place\" for resource with sensitive schema attributes\n   \u2193\n3. terraform show -json shows different sensitive_values in before vs. after\n   \u2193\n4. Root cause: Sensitivity metadata differs between before and after in JSON output\n   \u2193\n5. Before sensitivity: Includes schema marks (added at JSON output time)\n   After sensitivity: Includes schema marks (added at JSON output time)\n   Both appear different because schema marks were never in the planned change\n   \u2193\n6. Why schema marks are missing from planned change:\n   a) Refresh returns unmarked value from provider\n   b) Only variable-reference marks are reapplied (line 719)\n   c) State is encoded with incomplete marks (line 98)\n   d) Plan reads state with incomplete marks (lines 89-90)\n   e) Plan's BeforeValMarks only have variable marks, not schema marks\n   \u2193\n7. Why GetResource compensates:\n   - GetResource explicitly applies schema marks when reading from state (line 714-723)\n   - This is ONLY mechanism adding schema marks in normal flow\n   - But these marks are NOT captured in the plan itself\n   \u2193\n8. Why phantom diff appears:\n   - JSON output generation applies schema marks on-the-fly (lines 418-420, 446-449)\n   - Before value: Has dynamically-applied schema marks\n   - After value: Has dynamically-applied schema marks\n   - But from different sources (refreshed state vs. provider response)\n   - Even though underlying values are identical, mark structure differs\n   \u2193\n9. Why it only affects schema-sensitive attributes:\n   - Variable marks are preserved in state\n   - Schema marks are NOT preserved in state\n   - So only schema-sensitive attributes (without variable marks) lack marks in state\n   \u2193\n10. ROOT CAUSE: Asymmetry in mark persistence\n    - Sensitive variables: Marks persisted in state \u2713\n    - Schema sensitive attributes: Marks NOT persisted in state \u2717\n    - Compensating layer (GetResource) masks issue during evaluation\n    - JSON generation exposes issue by dynamically adding missing marks\n```\n\n---\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\nThe fix requires **ensuring schema-defined sensitive marks are persisted in state**, not applied only during evaluation or output generation.\n\n**Two approaches:**\n\n**Option A (Preferred): Apply schema marks at state encoding time**\n- Modify `node_resource_abstract_instance.go`'s `refresh()` method to apply schema marks before encoding\n- At line 717-720, after reapplying variable marks, also apply schema marks\n- This ensures state encodes complete sensitivity information\n- State decoding will then have complete marks\n- Eliminates need for compensating layer in evaluate.go\n- Eliminates dynamic mark application in JSON output\n\n**Option B: Capture schema marks in plan**\n- Modify `plan()` method to explicitly apply schema marks to `priorVal`\n- Encode schema marks into `BeforeValMarks` when creating the change\n- This ensures the planned change has complete mark information\n- Still requires changes to how marks are compared and stored\n\n### Diagnostic Steps\n\n1. **Enable trace logging** in `node_resource_abstract_instance.go`:\n   - Log `priorPaths` extracted at line 625\n   - Log marks on value after reapplying at line 719\n   - Compare against schema.ValueMarks() to see what's missing\n\n2. **Inspect state file** after refresh:\n   ```bash\n   terraform state show -json <resource> | jq '.current_state_object.sensitive_attributes'\n   ```\n   - Will only show paths for variable-marked attributes\n   - Should include schema-marked paths\n\n3. **Compare plan marks**:\n   ```bash\n   terraform show -json <plan-file> | jq '.resource_changes[].change | {before_sensitive, after_sensitive}'\n   ```\n   - Before will have no schema marks (from state)\n   - After will have schema marks (from evaluate.go)\n   - Difference indicates the phantom update\n\n4. **Test with schema-sensitive only** vs. **variable-sensitive only** attributes:\n   - Schema-sensitive-only: Phantom diff appears\n   - Variable-sensitive-only: No phantom diff (marks persisted)\n\n---\n\n## Additional Context\n\n### Why GetResource Compensates\n\nThe `GetResource()` method in `evaluate.go` (lines 714-723) is a **defensive compensating layer**. It ensures that when Terraform evaluates expressions that reference resource values from state, those values have schema-defined sensitivity marks applied. This prevents sensitive attributes from being accidentally logged or displayed during evaluation.\n\nHowever, **this compensation only applies to expression evaluation**, not to:\n- Plan change storage (`BeforeValMarks`, `AfterValMarks`)\n- State storage (`AttrSensitivePaths`)\n- Plan file output\n\n### Why JSON Output Exposes the Issue\n\nThe `jsonplan/plan.go` code (lines 418-420, 446-449) applies schema marks **at output time** because:\n1. It reads `BeforeValMarks` and `AfterValMarks` from the change, which have incomplete marks\n2. It detects the incompleteness via `schema.ContainsSensitive()`\n3. It dynamically adds missing schema marks for display purposes\n\nThis is a **second compensating layer** that only helps with JSON output, not with the core issue of incomplete mark persistence.\n\n### Historical Context\n\nThis design pattern suggests that at some point, the `GetResource()` compensation was sufficient. The system likely worked when:\n- Resource values were always read via `GetResource()` for comparison\n- JSON output was generated more directly from evaluated values\n\nThe issue emerged when:\n- Direct state comparisons started being used for plan generation\n- JSON output generation was refactored to use stored `ValMarks` instead of evaluated values\n",

This creates the asymmetry: values read **via GetResource** have schema marks added, but values read **directly from state** in the plan path do not.\n\n5. **`internal/command/jsonplan/plan.go`, `MarshalResourceChange()` method (lines 417-420, 446-449)**: When generating JSON output for display, schema marks are applied on-the-fly to both before and after values. Refresh Path \u2013 Incomplete Mark Extraction (node_resource_abstract_instance.go:620-722)**\n\n```go\n// Line 623-626: Extract marks BEFORE sending to provider\nvar priorPaths []cty.PathValueMarks\nif priorVal.ContainsMarked() {\n    priorVal, priorPaths = priorVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n}\n// priorPaths only contains marks from sensitive variables, NOT schema\n\n// Line 717-720: Reapply marks AFTER provider returns\nif len(priorPaths) > 0 {\n    ret.Value = ret.Value.MarkWithPaths(priorPaths)\n}\n// Schema marks are NOT reapplied here\n```\n\n**Issue**: `priorPaths` only has marks from sensitive variable references. Provider schema declares sensitive attributes are never added at this point.\n\n---\n\n**2. State Encoding \u2013 Missing Schema Marks (instance_object.go:94-137)**\n\n```go\nfunc (o *ResourceInstanceObject) Encode(ty cty.Type, schemaVersion uint64) (*ResourceInstanceObjectSrc, error) {\n    // Line 98: Extract existing marks\n    val, pvm := o.Value.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n\n    // ... process value ...\n\n    // Line 131: Save only the marks that are on the value\n    AttrSensitivePaths:  pvm,  // Missing schema marks!\n}\n```\n\n**Issue**: Only marks present in the value are persisted. Schema-defined sensitive marks are never in the value because the refresh path never adds them.\n\n---\n\n**3. State Decoding \u2013 Restore Incomplete Marks (instance_object_src.go:77-104)**\n\n```go\nfunc (os *ResourceInstanceObjectSrc) Decode(ty cty.Type) (*ResourceInstanceObject, error) {\n    val, err := ctyjson.Unmarshal(os.AttrsJSON, ty)\n    if os.AttrSensitivePaths != nil {\n        val = val.MarkWithPaths(os.AttrSensitivePaths)  // Only has variable marks\n    }\n    return &ResourceInstanceObject{Value: val, ...}, nil\n}\n```\n\n**Issue**: Reapplies only the incomplete marks that were stored.\n\n---\n\n**4. Evaluator Compensation \u2013 Schema Marks Applied at Expression Evaluation Time (evaluate.go:714-723)**\n\n```go\n// When reading from state for planned resources (lines 714-723)\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    var marks []cty.PathValueMarks\n    val, marks = val.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n    marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(val, nil)...)  // ADD schema marks here\n    val = val.MarkWithPaths(marks)\n}\ninstances[key] = val\n```\n\n**Issue**: This is a compensating mechanism that adds schema marks during **evaluation** (when reading from state for expression purposes), but these marks are **not** part of the planned change or state storage. This is the ONLY place schema marks are applied in the normal flow.\n\n---\n\n**5. JSON Output Generation \u2013 Dynamic Schema Mark Addition (jsonplan/plan.go:417-420, 446-449)**\n\n```go\n// For Before value (line 417-425):\nmarks := rc.BeforeValMarks  // Only has variable marks from the plan\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(changeV.Before, nil)...)  // Add schema marks here\n}\nbs := jsonstate.SensitiveAsBool(changeV.Before.MarkWithPaths(marks))\nbeforeSensitive, err := ctyjson.Marshal(bs, bs.Type())\n\n// For After value (line 446-449):\nmarks := rc.AfterValMarks  // Only has variable marks from the plan\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(changeV.After, nil)...)  // Add schema marks here\n}\nas := jsonstate.SensitiveAsBool(changeV.After.MarkWithPaths(marks))\nafterSensitive, err := ctyjson.Marshal(as, as.Type())\n```\n\n**Issue**: Schema marks are applied at JSON output time, making the before value appear to have sensitivity information that was never persisted in the plan. The difference in before vs. after sensitivity (in marks only, not in values) appears as a change to the user.\n\n---\n\n**6. Plan Phase \u2013 Incomplete Mark Comparison (node_resource_abstract_instance.go:1208-1210)**\n\n```go\n// Check if marks differ even though values are equal\nif action == plans.NoOp && !marksEqual(filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths), priorPaths) {\n    action = plans.Update\n}\n```\n\n**Issue**: This compares `unmarkedPaths` (marks from config) against `priorPaths` (marks from state, missing schema marks). Neither has schema marks, so for schema-sensitive attributes with no variable marks, they appear equal when they shouldn't.\n\n---\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`** \u2013 Refresh path, plan path:\n   - `refresh()` method: Extracts and reapplies incomplete marks\n   - `plan()` method: Uses incomplete marks for comparison\n   - Does not apply schema marks to prior values\n\n2. **`internal/states/instance_object.go`** \u2013 State serialization:\n   - `Encode()` method: Serializes incomplete marks to state file\n\n3. **`internal/states/instance_object_src.go`** \u2013 State deserialization:\n   - `Decode()` method: Restores incomplete marks from state\n\n4. **`internal/terraform/evaluate.go`** \u2013 Expression evaluation:\n   - `GetResource()` method: Applies schema marks when reading state for evaluation (compensating mechanism)\n\n5. **`internal/command/jsonplan/plan.go`** \u2013 JSON plan output:\n   - `MarshalResourceChange()` method: Dynamically applies schema marks at output time\n\n6. **`internal/terraform/marks.go`** \u2013 Utility functions:\n   - `marksEqual()`: Used for comparing incomplete mark sets\n   - `filterMarks()`: Filters inapplicable marks\n\n---\n\n## Causal Chain\n\n```\n1. SYMPTOM: terraform plan shows phantom in-place update even with no config changes\n   \u2193\n2. User sees \"will be updated in-place\" for resource with sensitive schema attributes\n   \u2193\n3. terraform show -json shows different sensitive_values in before vs. after\n   \u2193\n4. Root cause: Sensitivity metadata differs between before and after in JSON output\n   \u2193\n5. Before sensitivity: Includes schema marks (added at JSON output time)\n   After sensitivity: Includes schema marks (added at JSON output time)\n   Both appear different because schema marks were never in the planned change\n   \u2193\n6. Why phantom diff appears:\n   - JSON output generation applies schema marks on-the-fly (lines 418-420, 446-449)\n   - Before value: Has dynamically-applied schema marks\n   - After value: Has dynamically-applied schema marks\n   - But from different sources (refreshed state vs. provider response)\n   - Even though underlying values are identical, mark structure differs\n   \u2193\n9. JSON generation exposes issue by dynamically adding missing marks\n```\n\n---\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\nThe fix requires **ensuring schema-defined sensitive marks are persisted in state**, not applied only during evaluation or output generation.\n\n**Two approaches:**\n\n**Option A (Preferred): Apply schema marks at state encoding time**\n- Modify `node_resource_abstract_instance.go`'s `refresh()` method to apply schema marks before encoding\n- At line 717-720, after reapplying variable marks, also apply schema marks\n- This ensures state encodes complete sensitivity information\n- State decoding will then have complete marks\n- Eliminates need for compensating layer in evaluate.go\n- Eliminates dynamic mark application in JSON output\n\n**Option B: Capture schema marks in plan**\n- Modify `plan()` method to explicitly apply schema marks to `priorVal`\n- Encode schema marks into `BeforeValMarks` when creating the change\n- This ensures the planned change has complete mark information\n- Still requires changes to how marks are compared and stored\n\n### Diagnostic Steps\n\n1. **Enable trace logging** in `node_resource_abstract_instance.go`:\n   - Log `priorPaths` extracted at line 625\n   - Log marks on value after reapplying at line 719\n   - Compare against schema.ValueMarks() to see what's missing\n\n2. **Inspect state file** after refresh:\n   ```bash\n   terraform state show -json <resource> | jq '.current_state_object.sensitive_attributes'\n   ```\n   - Will only show paths for variable-marked attributes\n   - Should include schema-marked paths\n\n3. **Compare plan marks**:\n   ```bash\n   terraform show -json <plan-file> | jq '.resource_changes[].change | {before_sensitive, after_sensitive}'\n   ```\n   - Before will have no schema marks (from state)\n   - After will have schema marks (from evaluate.go)\n   - Difference indicates the phantom update\n\n4. **Test with schema-sensitive only** vs. **variable-sensitive only** attributes:\n   - Schema-sensitive-only: Phantom diff appears\n   - Variable-sensitive-only: No phantom diff (marks persisted)\n\n---\n\n## Additional Context\n\n### Why GetResource Compensates\n\nThe `GetResource()` method in `evaluate.go` (lines 714-723) is a **defensive compensating layer**. It ensures that when Terraform evaluates expressions that reference resource values from state, those values have schema-defined sensitivity marks applied. This prevents sensitive attributes from being accidentally logged or displayed during evaluation.\n\nHowever, **this compensation only applies to expression evaluation**, not to:\n- Plan change storage (`BeforeValMarks`, `AfterValMarks`)\n- State storage (`AttrSensitivePaths`)\n- Plan file output\n\n### Why JSON Output Exposes the Issue\n\nThe `jsonplan/plan.go` code (lines 418-420, 446-449) applies schema marks **at output time** because:\n1. The system likely worked when:\n- Resource values were always read via `GetResource()` for comparison\n- JSON output was generated more directly from evaluated values\n\nThe issue emerged when:\n- Direct state comparisons started being used for plan generation\n- JSON output generation was refactored to use stored `ValMarks` instead of evaluated values\n",

# Investigation Report: Phantom In-Place Updates for Resources with Sensitive Attributes

## Summary

Terraform generates phantom in-place update diffs for resources with provider-schema-defined sensitive attributes because of an asymmetry in how sensitivity marks flow through the system. The issue stems from **incomplete sensitivity mark persistence in state**: when resource values are refreshed and stored, only marks from sensitive variable references are saved, not marks from the provider schema itself. During plan generation, schema marks are applied dynamically to the JSON output for display purposes, creating an apparent difference in sensitivity between before and after values even though the underlying attribute values are identical.

---

## Root Cause

**Incomplete sensitivity mark storage at state serialization boundary.**

The root cause is located in the **state refresh-to-storage pipeline**, specifically:

1. **`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`, `refresh()` method (lines 620-722)**: When a resource is refreshed from the provider, marks extracted before sending to the provider (`priorPaths` at line 625) only contain marks from sensitive variables (e.g., `var.db_password` marked as sensitive). These are **not** the provider schema's declared sensitive attributes.

2. **`internal/states/instance_object.go`, `Encode()` method (line 98)**: When encoding the refreshed value for storage, `UnmarkDeepWithPaths()` extracts **only the marks currently on the value**. Since schema-defined sensitive marks were never added to the refreshed value (the provider returns unmarked values and only variable marks are reapplied), the schema marks are **not** present in the encoded state.

3. **`internal/states/instance_object_src.go`, `Decode()` method (lin
... (truncated)
